Arjuna Vishada Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 1.1

‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö | ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§µ‡§É |
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§ ‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø ||

Dhritarashtra uvƒÅcha: Dharmakshetre Kurukshetre samavetƒÅ yuyutsava·∏•,
MƒÅmaka·∏• PƒÅ·πá·∏çavƒÅ≈õchaiva kimakurvata Sa√±jaya.

Symbolism: Sets the stage for the epic battle and highlights the moral conflict of dharma.

English: Dhritarashtra said: O Sanjaya, assembled in the holy land of Kurukshetra, what did my sons and the sons of Pandu do, eager to fight?

Meaning: Dhritarashtra inquires about the actions of the warriors, setting the stage for the battle.

Full Explanation: This verse introduces the battlefield of Kurukshetra and the tension before war. It reflects the concern of a father observing his sons and highlights the moral and familial dilemmas.

Arjuna Vishada Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 1.28

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö | ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç |
‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ||

Sƒ´danti mama gƒÅtrƒÅ·πái mukha·πÅ cha pari≈õu·π£yati.

Symbolism: Arjuna is overwhelmed with sorrow seeing his relatives ready to fight.

English: Arjuna said: O Krishna, seeing my kinsmen assembled for battle, my limbs fail and my mouth dries.

Meaning: Arjuna experiences intense sorrow and hesitation at the thought of fighting his own family and friends.

Full Explanation: This verse marks the beginning of Arjuna‚Äôs emotional crisis. He sees the battlefield full of his loved ones, and the sense of duty is clouded by compassion and grief.

Arjuna Vishada Yoga

Symbolism: Arjuna‚Äôs mind is confused and memory fails him due to grief and compassion.

Arjuna Vishada Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 1.30

‡§® ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§£ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø |
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ß‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ||

Svajana·πÅ hatvƒÅ sukha·πÅ vƒÅ dhana·πÅ vƒÅ svarga·πÅ prƒÅptu·πÅ vƒÅ.

Symbolism: Arjuna refuses to gain wealth, pleasure, or heaven at the cost of killing loved ones.

English: I do not desire heaven, wealth, or pleasure if it comes from killing my own kinsmen.

Meaning: Moral principles override material desires for Arjuna.

Full Explanation: Arjuna emphasizes compassion and the ethical dilemma of war against family. This verse deepens the emotional and moral crisis.

Arjuna Vishada Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 1.47

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§´‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§® |
‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ||

Karma·πáyevƒÅdhikƒÅraste mƒÅ phale·π£u kadƒÅcana,
MƒÅ karmaphalaheturbh≈´rmƒÅ te sa·πÖgo'stvakarma·πái.

Symbolism: Emphasizes performing one‚Äôs duty without attachment to results; foundational teaching of karma yoga.

English: You have the right to perform your prescribed duties, but you are not entitled to the fruits of your actions. Do not let the fruits be your motivation, nor let your attachment be to inaction.

Meaning: Duty (karma) is paramount; do not be attached to success or failure.

Full Explanation: This verse introduces the central principle of karma yoga ‚Äî performing duties selflessly without attachment to outcomes. It addresses Arjuna‚Äôs dilemma of action versus inaction and lays the foundation for Krishna‚Äôs guidance throughout the Gita.

Sankhya Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 2.13

‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡•á ‡§ï‡•å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•å‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§∞‡§æ |
‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§® ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ||

Dehino'smin yathƒÅ dehe kaumƒÅra·πÅ yauvana·πÅ jarƒÅ,
TathƒÅ dehƒÅntaraprƒÅptir dhƒ´ras tatra na muhyati.

Symbolism: The soul is eternal and unchanging; the body is temporary like childhood, youth, and old age.

English: As the soul passes through childhood, youth, and old age in the body, so it passes into another body at death.

Meaning: The soul is eternal; it is never destroyed by physical death.

Full Explanation: This verse explains the eternal nature of the soul. Just as the body undergoes changes and aging, the soul moves from one body to another, remaining untouched by death. This teaching encourages performing duties without fear.

Sankhya Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 2.19

‡§Ø ‡§è‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç |
‡§â‡§≠‡•å ‡§§‡•å ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ||

Ya ena·πÅ vetti hantƒÅra·πÅ yashchaina·πÅ manyate hatam,
Ubhau tau na vijƒÅnƒ´to nƒÅya·πÅ hanti na hanyate.

Symbolism: The soul cannot be killed nor does it kill; it is eternal and indestructible.

English: Those who think the soul kills, or the soul is killed, do not understand its eternal nature; it neither kills nor can be killed.

Meaning: The soul is immortal and beyond physical harm.

Full Explanation: This verse reinforces the concept that the soul is eternal, indestructible, and beyond birth and death. It is not affected by physical events and thus provides Arjuna the philosophical basis to face battle without attachment.

Sankhya Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 2.31

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§É ||

Svadharme nidhana·πÅ ≈õreya·∏•, paradharmo bhayƒÅvaha·∏•.

Symbolism: Performing one‚Äôs own duty is always better, even if it involves risk; following another‚Äôs duty leads to fear and failure.

English: It is better to die in performing one‚Äôs own duty than to follow another‚Äôs duty, which is fraught with fear.

Meaning: Duty according to one‚Äôs nature (svadharma) is superior to duties alien to one‚Äôs role.

Full Explanation: Krishna advises Arjuna that adhering to his own dharma as a warrior, even with risks, is noble. Acting against one‚Äôs natural duties causes fear, confusion, and spiritual degradation.

MƒÅ karmaphalaheturbh≈´rmƒÅ te sa·πÖgo'stvakarma·πái.

Symbolism: Perform your duties without attachment to results; foundational principle of Karma Yoga.

English: You have the right to perform your duties, but not to the results. Do not let the results be your motivation, nor attachment to inaction.

Meaning: Focus on duty, not outcomes; act selflessly.

Full Explanation: This central verse of Karma Yoga instructs Arjuna to perform actions with dedication and detachment. Success or failure is not the concern; the focus is on righteous action, which purifies the mind and soul.

Bhagavad Gita 2.50

‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§π ‡§â‡§≠‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á |
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Å ‡§ï‡•å‡§∂‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç ||

Buddhiyukto jahƒÅtƒ´ha ubhe suk·πõta-du·π£k·πõte,
TasmƒÅd yogƒÅya yujyasva yoga·∏• karmasu kau≈õalam.

Symbolism: Equanimity in action‚Äîsuccess and failure are treated equally; skill in performing duties is yoga.

English: The one who is endowed with wisdom abandons both good and bad deeds in this life; therefore, dedicate yourself to yoga. Skillful performance of action is yoga.

Meaning: Treat success and failure equally; skill in performing duty is true yoga.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes that yoga is not just meditation‚Äîit is also perfect action performed with wisdom and detachment. A wise person acts skillfully without attachment to results, treating all outcomes with equanimity.

Sankhya Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 2.70

‡§Ü‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§ö‡§≤‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç |
‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§∏ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä ||

ƒÄp≈´ryamƒÅ·πáam achala-prati·π£·π≠ha·πÅ samudram ƒÅpa·∏• pravi≈õanti yadvat,
Tadvat kƒÅmƒÅ ya·πÅ pravi≈õanti sarve sa ≈õƒÅntim ƒÅpnoti na kƒÅmakƒÅmƒ´.

Symbolism: Like rivers entering the ocean without disturbing it, a wise person remains detached and peaceful.

English: Just as the waters flow into the ocean without disturbing it, the desires of a wise person, who is detached, do not disturb his peace.

Meaning: Detachment leads to inner peace and freedom from desires.

Full Explanation: This verse illustrates the ideal of a person who remains undisturbed by desires and external events. The wise soul, like the ocean, absorbs all experiences calmly, achieving equanimity and serenity.

Karma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 3.5

‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•à‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•á |
‡§® ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø ||

Na karma·πáƒÅm anƒÅrambhƒÅn nai·π£karmya·πÅ puru·π£o'≈õnute,
Na ca sannyasƒÅd eva siddhi·πÅ samadhigacchati.

Symbolism: The soul cannot remain inactive; action is essential for life and spiritual progress.

English: The soul cannot avoid action entirely, nor can perfection be attained merely by renunciation.

Meaning: Inaction is impossible; one must act according to dharma.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that everyone is compelled to act, whether consciously or unconsciously. True spiritual advancement requires performing duty, not merely renouncing action.

Karma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 3.7

‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§∏ ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á |
‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§® ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É ||

Yastu karmaphala-tyƒÅgƒ´ sa tyƒÅgƒ´tabhidhƒ´yate,
Sa sannyƒÅsƒ´ ca yogƒ´ ca na niragnir na cƒÅkriya·∏•.

Symbolism: One who renounces the fruits of action is both a yogi and a true renunciant; selfless action is the essence of karma yoga.

English: One who renounces the fruits of action is called a true renunciant and a yogi; action without attachment is essential.

Meaning: Selfless action is the path of karma yoga and true renunciation.

Full Explanation: Krishna teaches that mere abandonment of duties is not renunciation. A true yogi performs duties without attachment to results, integrating renunciation and action.

Karma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 3.8

‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§É |
‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§§‡•á ‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§É ||

Niyata·πÅ kuru karma tva·πÅ karma jyƒÅyo hy akarma·πáa·∏•,
≈öarƒ´rayƒÅtrƒÅpi ca te na prasiddhyed akarma·πáa·∏•.

Symbolism: Performing prescribed duties is better than inaction; even survival requires action.

English: Perform your prescribed duties; action is superior to inaction. Even your bodily maintenance cannot happen without action.

Meaning: Duty must be performed; inaction is not practical or righteous.

Full Explanation: Krishna advises Arjuna that abstaining from action is impossible, as even survival requires work. Performing one‚Äôs duty with discipline is essential for personal and social balance.

Karma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 3.16

‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§π ‡§Ø: |
‡§Ö‡§ò‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ò‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ||

Eva·πÅ pravartita·πÅ cakra·πÅ nƒÅnuvartayatƒ´ha ya·∏•,
AghƒÅyur indriyƒÅrƒÅmo mogha·πÅ pƒÅrtha sa jƒ´vati.

Symbolism: Neglecting one‚Äôs duties disrupts society and leads to wasteful life.

English: Whoever neglects the order of duties set in society, desiring only sense pleasures, lives a wasted life.

Meaning: Ignoring one‚Äôs duties harms oneself and society.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes the interdependence of society. Everyone has a role; neglecting duties for selfish pleasure disrupts the cosmic and social balance, leading to a life without fulfillment.

Karma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 3.19

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞ |
‡§Ö‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É ||

TasmƒÅd asakta·∏• satata·πÅ kƒÅrya·πÅ karma samƒÅchara,
Asakto hy ƒÅcaran karma paramƒÅpnoti p≈´ru·π£a·∏•.

Symbolism: Perform duties without attachment; selfless action leads to the highest spiritual attainment.

English: Therefore, perform your prescribed duties constantly, without attachment. By doing so without attachment, one attains the highest.

Meaning: Selfless, detached action is the essence of karma yoga and leads to perfection.

Full Explanation: Krishna instructs that attachment binds the soul. By performing duty with detachment and focus, one transcends selfishness and approaches spiritual liberation.

Karma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 3.30

‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡§æ |
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§´‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§® ||

Mayi sarvƒÅ·πái karmƒÅ·πái sannyasyƒÅdhyƒÅtma-cetasƒÅ,
NirvƒÅ·πáam avƒÅpsyasi mƒÅ phale·π£u kadƒÅcana.

Symbolism: Dedicate all actions to Krishna; attachment to results hinders spiritual progress.

English: Surrender all your actions to Me with a spiritual mind. By doing so, you will attain liberation and never be bound by the fruits.

Meaning: Offer all actions to Krishna; detach from results to achieve liberation.

Full Explanation: Krishna instructs Arjuna to dedicate every act to the divine. By abandoning attachment to outcomes and focusing on God-conscious action, one attains freedom, equanimity, and spiritual fulfillment.

Jnana Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 4.7

‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§ |
‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç ||

YadƒÅ yadƒÅ hi dharmasya glƒÅnir bhavati bhƒÅrata,
AbhyutthƒÅnam adharmasya tadƒÅtmƒÅna·πÅ s·πõjƒÅmy aham.

Symbolism: God incarnates whenever righteousness declines to restore dharma and cosmic balance.

English: Whenever there is a decline of righteousness and rise of unrighteousness, I manifest Myself.

Meaning: God incarnates to protect dharma and restore moral order.

Full Explanation: Krishna reassures Arjuna that the divine always intervenes when dharma is threatened, maintaining cosmic and social balance through incarnations.

Jnana Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 4.8

‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç |

ParitrƒÅ·πáƒÅya sƒÅdh≈´nƒÅ·πÅ vinƒÅ≈õƒÅya ca du·π£k·πõtƒÅm,
Dharma-sa·πÅsthƒÅpanƒÅrthƒÅya sambhavƒÅmi yuge yuge.

Symbolism: God appears in every age to protect the virtuous, destroy evil, and establish dharma.

English: To protect the virtuous, destroy the wicked, and establish dharma, I manifest in every age.

Meaning: God intervenes to maintain righteousness and balance in the world.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that divine incarnations have a clear purpose: uphold moral order, eliminate evil, and support the virtuous, ensuring cosmic harmony.

Symbolism: The four varnas are created by God based on qualities and duties; one should understand their role in life.

English: The four varnas were created by Me based on qualities and duties. Know Me as the eternal creator beyond action.

Meaning: Duties in life are aligned with one‚Äôs nature and qualities.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains the division of society into four varnas is based on individual qualities and work. Understanding one‚Äôs role and performing duties accordingly is essential for harmony.

Karma·πáai eva hi sa·πÅsiddhim ƒÅsti na manorathe·πáa vƒÅ,
Na hi kaunteya sa·πÅsiddhi·πÅ paryapnoti kuta·∏• karmajam.

Symbolism: Knowledge alone is not enough; wisdom combined with action leads to perfection.

English: Perfection is attained through action, not merely desire or knowledge alone.

Meaning: Practical action aligned with knowledge is essential.

Full Explanation: Krishna teaches that wisdom must be applied through disciplined action. Knowledge without practice does not lead to spiritual perfection.

Jnana Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 4.33

‡§∏ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§É |
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç ||

Sa tu yogyam ito 'rjuna j√±ƒÅna-yukta·∏• karma-k·πõttama·∏•,
Sarva-karma-phala-tyƒÅgƒ´ j√±ƒÅna-sannyasta-karma-k·πõt.

Symbolism: A wise person performs actions without attachment to results, combining renunciation and knowledge.

English: But the wise person, endowed with knowledge, performs action in accordance with duty, renouncing the fruits of all actions.

Meaning: Selfless action guided by knowledge leads to liberation.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes that the spiritually knowledgeable person acts without desire for personal gain. Such detachment ensures that actions are aligned with dharma while avoiding karmic bondage.

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•: ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§® ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§ø‡§§ ‡§®‡§ø:‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ì‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•á ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡•§

Telugu: ‡∞ï‡∞æ‡∞®‡±Ä ‡∞ú‡±ç‡∞û‡∞æ‡∞®‡∞Ç ‡∞ó‡∞≤ ‡∞µ‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞ï‡±ç‡∞§‡∞ø ‡∞ï‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞§‡∞µ‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞æ‡∞®‡±Å‡∞∏‡∞æ‡∞∞‡∞Ç ‡∞ï‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞§‡∞µ‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞Ç ‡∞ö‡±á‡∞∏‡±ç‡∞§‡∞æ‡∞°‡±Å ‡∞Æ‡∞∞‡∞ø‡∞Ø‡±Å ‡∞Ö‡∞®‡±ç‡∞®‡∞ø ‡∞ï‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞Æ‡∞≤ ‡∞´‡∞≤‡∞æ‡∞≤‡∞®‡±Å ‡∞µ‡∞¶‡∞ø‡∞≤‡∞ø‡∞µ‡±á‡∞∏‡±ç‡∞§‡∞æ‡∞°‡±Å.

‡∞Ö‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞•‡∞Ç: ‡∞ú‡±ç‡∞û‡∞æ‡∞®‡∞Ç ‡∞¶‡±ç‡∞µ‡∞æ‡∞∞‡∞æ ‡∞Æ‡∞æ‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞ó‡∞®‡∞ø‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞¶‡±á‡∞∂‡∞Ç ‡∞Ö‡∞Ø‡∞ø‡∞® ‡∞∏‡±ç‡∞µ‡∞æ‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞•‡∞∞‡∞π‡∞ø‡∞§ ‡∞ï‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞§‡∞µ‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞Ç ‡∞µ‡∞ø‡∞Æ‡±Å‡∞ï‡±ç‡∞§‡∞ø‡∞ï‡∞ø ‡∞¶‡∞æ‡∞∞‡∞ø ‡∞ö‡±Ç‡∞™‡∞ø‡∞∏‡±ç‡∞§‡±Å‡∞Ç‡∞¶‡∞ø.

Jnana Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 4.34

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ |
‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡§É ||

Tad viddhi pra·πáipƒÅtena paripra≈õnena sevayƒÅ,
Upadek·π£yanti te j√±ƒÅna·πÅ j√±ƒÅnina·∏• tattva-dar≈õina·∏•.

Symbolism: Humble devotion and service to a wise teacher is the path to spiritual knowledge.

English: Learn the truth by humbly approaching a teacher, asking questions, and serving them; the wise, who see the truth, will impart knowledge.

Meaning: True knowledge comes from a combination of humility, inquiry, and guidance from the realized.

Full Explanation: Krishna instructs Arjuna that spiritual wisdom cannot be acquired through ego or superficial study. A sincere seeker must approach a knowledgeable teacher with respect, ask questions, and serve. Only then will the teacher reveal the deeper truths.

Telugu: ‡∞®‡∞ø‡∞ú‡∞æ‡∞®‡∞ø‡∞ú‡∞æ‡∞®‡±ç‡∞®‡∞ø ‡∞§‡±Ü‡∞≤‡±Å‡∞∏‡±Å‡∞ï‡±ã‡∞µ‡∞°‡∞æ‡∞®‡∞ø‡∞ï‡∞ø, ‡∞ó‡±Å‡∞∞‡±Å‡∞µ‡±Å‡∞®‡∞ø ‡∞∏‡∞®‡±ç‡∞Æ‡∞æ‡∞®‡∞Ç‡∞§‡±ã ‡∞∏‡∞Æ‡±Ä‡∞™‡∞ø‡∞Ç‡∞ö‡∞Ç‡∞°‡∞ø, ‡∞™‡±ç‡∞∞‡∞∂‡±ç‡∞®‡∞≤‡±Å ‡∞Ö‡∞°‡∞ó‡∞Ç‡∞°‡∞ø, ‡∞∏‡±á‡∞µ ‡∞ö‡±á‡∞Ø‡∞Ç‡∞°‡∞ø; ‡∞ú‡±ç‡∞û‡∞æ‡∞®‡∞Ç ‡∞ó‡∞≤‡∞µ‡∞æ‡∞∞‡±Å ‡∞Æ‡±Ä‡∞ï‡±Å ‡∞ú‡±ç‡∞û‡∞æ‡∞®‡∞Ç ‡∞Ö‡∞Ç‡∞¶‡∞ø‡∞∏‡±ç‡∞§‡∞æ‡∞∞‡±Å.

‡∞µ‡∞ø‡∞µ‡∞∞‡∞£: ‡∞ï‡±É‡∞∑‡±ç‡∞£‡±Å‡∞°‡±Å ‡∞Ö‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞ú‡±Å‡∞®‡±Å‡∞®‡∞ø ‡∞∏‡±Ç‡∞ö‡∞ø‡∞∏‡±ç‡∞§‡±Å‡∞®‡±ç‡∞®‡∞æ‡∞∞, ‡∞Ü‡∞ß‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞æ‡∞§‡±ç‡∞Æ‡∞ø‡∞ï ‡∞ú‡±ç‡∞û‡∞æ‡∞®‡∞Ç ‡∞Ö‡∞π‡∞Ç‡∞ï‡∞æ‡∞∞‡∞Ç ‡∞≤‡±á‡∞¶‡∞æ ‡∞â‡∞™‡∞∞‡∞ø‡∞§‡∞≤ ‡∞Ö‡∞ß‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞Ø‡∞®‡∞Ç‡∞§‡±ã ‡∞™‡±ä‡∞Ç‡∞¶‡∞≤‡±á‡∞Æ‡±Å. ‡∞®‡∞ø‡∞ú‡∞Æ‡±à‡∞® ‡∞Ö‡∞≠‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞•‡∞ø ‡∞ó‡±å‡∞∞‡∞µ‡∞Ç‡∞§‡±ã ‡∞ó‡±Å‡∞∞‡±Å‡∞µ‡±Å‡∞®‡∞ø ‡∞∏‡∞Ç‡∞™‡±ç‡∞∞‡∞¶‡∞ø‡∞Ç‡∞ö‡∞æ‡∞≤‡∞ø, ‡∞™‡±ç‡∞∞‡∞∂‡±ç‡∞®‡∞≤‡±Å ‡∞Ö‡∞°‡∞ó‡∞æ‡∞≤‡∞ø ‡∞Æ‡∞∞‡∞ø‡∞Ø‡±Å ‡∞∏‡±á‡∞µ ‡∞ö‡±á‡∞Ø‡∞æ‡∞≤‡∞ø. ‡∞Ö‡∞™‡±ç‡∞™‡±Å‡∞°‡±Å ‡∞Æ‡∞æ‡∞§‡±ç‡∞∞‡∞Æ‡±á ‡∞ó‡±Å‡∞∞‡±Å‡∞µ‡±Å ‡∞≤‡±ã‡∞§‡±à‡∞® ‡∞∏‡∞§‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞æ‡∞≤‡∞®‡±Å ‡∞µ‡±Ü‡∞≤‡±ç‡∞≤‡∞°‡∞ø‡∞∏‡±ç‡∞§‡∞æ‡∞∞‡±Å.

Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 5.2

‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∏‡§ø |
‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•á‡§Ω‡§• ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§‡§É ‡§Æ‡§Æ ||

SannyƒÅsa·πÅ karma·πáƒÅ·πÅ k·πõ·π£·πáa punar-yoga·πÅ ca ≈õa·πÅsasi,
Yacchreya·∏• sannyƒÅse 'tha yoge ca samƒÅpto mata·∏• mama.

Symbolism: Both renunciation and selfless action lead to liberation, but karma yoga is superior for most people.

English: Krishna, you praise both renunciation and yoga, but I consider karma yoga superior.

Meaning: Selfless action (karma yoga) is the more practical path for most to attain liberation.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that while renunciation is spiritual, performing duties without attachment is superior in guiding most people toward freedom from material bondage.

Hindi: ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£, ‡§Ü‡§™ ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó ‡§¶‡•ã‡§®‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç, ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§† ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ç‡§Å‡•§

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•: ‡§®‡§ø:‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡§ø‡§è ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó ‡§π‡•à‡•§

‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡§£: ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§¨‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï ‡§π‡•à, ‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡§ø‡§® ‡§¨‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≠‡•å‡§§‡§ø‡§ï ‡§¨‡§Ç‡§ß‡§®‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•Ä ‡§ì‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•á ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡•§

Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 5.10

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§É |
‡§≤‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§® ‡§∏ ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∏‡§æ ||

Brahma·πáyƒÅdhƒÅya karmƒÅ·πái sa·πÖga·πÅ tyaktvƒÅ karoti ya·∏•,
Lipyate na sa pƒÅpebhya·∏• padma-patram ivƒÅmbhasƒÅ.

Symbolism: Performing duties without attachment leaves one untouched by sin, like a lotus leaf is untouched by water.

English: One who dedicates all actions to Brahman, abandoning attachment, is not tainted by sin, just like a lotus leaf remains untouched by water.

Meaning: Selfless action protects one from karmic bondage.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes that surrendering the results of action to the divine while performing one‚Äôs duties purifies the mind and keeps the soul unaffected by the material consequences of actions.

Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 5.12

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§É |
‡§∏ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç ||

Karma·πáy akarma ya·∏• pa≈õyed akarma·πái cha karma ya·∏•,
Sa buddhimƒÅn manu·π£ye·π£u sa yukta·∏• k·πõtsna-karma-k·πõt.

Symbolism: Wisdom lies in understanding what actions to perform and what to renounce; such a person is truly balanced.

English: The wise see inaction in action and action in inaction; they are balanced and perform all duties efficiently.

Meaning: True wisdom is recognizing the spiritual essence behind action and renunciation.

Full Explanation: Krishna teaches that a spiritually aware person acts without attachment, understanding the inner significance of duty, and performs all actions without being bound by them.

Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 5.18

‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•á ‡§ó‡§µ‡§ø ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§ø |
‡§∂‡•Å‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ö ‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§æ: ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§æ‡§É ||

VidyƒÅ-vinaya-sampanne brƒÅhma·πáe gavi hastini,
≈öuni chaiva ≈õvapƒÅke cha pa·πá·∏çitƒÅ·∏• samadar≈õanƒÅ·∏•.

Symbolism: The truly wise see all beings equally, regardless of social status or species.

English: The learned see a wise person equally in a learned Brahmin, a cow, an elephant, a dog, and even in a dog-eater.

Meaning: True wisdom perceives the same divine essence in all beings.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes equality and non-discrimination. A spiritually realized person sees all creatures, high or low, gentle or harsh, as manifestations of the same consciousness.

Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 5.29

‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§≤‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç |
‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§®‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç ||

Yato yato ni≈õcarati mana≈õ cha√±calam asthiram,
Tatastato niyamyaitad ƒÅtmanyeva va≈õa·πÅ nayet.

Symbolism: Control of the mind leads to discipline and inner peace.

English: Wherever the mind wanders, a wise person must restrain it and bring it under control.

Meaning: Mind control is essential for spiritual discipline.

Full Explanation: Krishna teaches that the mind is naturally restless. A disciplined seeker must continuously bring the mind back, focusing it on the self or the divine, to maintain inner stability and progress in yoga.

Karma Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 5.35

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§æ‡§É |
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ||

Brahma·πái sthito 'rjuna na tva·πÅ ≈õoka·πÅ kuru k·π£vabhƒÅ·∏•,
Sarva-karma-phala-tyƒÅgƒ´ santu·π£·π≠o mayƒÅ tathƒÅ.

Symbolism: Renouncing the fruits of all actions and being established in Brahman leads to supreme peace and contentment.

English: Arjuna, being established in Brahman and renouncing the fruits of action, do not grieve; such a person remains satisfied.

Meaning: Detachment and realization of the self bring supreme contentment.

Full Explanation: Krishna reassures Arjuna that surrendering the results of action while performing duties and remaining anchored in the divine leads to peace and freedom from sorrow.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.5

‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç |
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§µ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§µ ‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ||

Uddhared ƒÅtmanƒÅt mƒÅtmƒÅnam nƒÅtmƒÅnam avasƒÅdayet,
ƒÄtmaiva hy ƒÅtmano bandhur ƒÅtmaiva ripur ƒÅtmana·∏•.

Symbolism: Self-upliftment and self-discipline; the soul is one‚Äôs own friend and enemy.

English: One must elevate oneself by one‚Äôs own mind, not degrade oneself; the self is one‚Äôs own friend or enemy.

Meaning: Self-discipline and inner effort determine liberation.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes personal responsibility. By controlling and uplifting one‚Äôs own mind, a person can achieve spiritual growth. Neglecting this leads to self-defeat.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.6

‡§Ö‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§µ ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ||

Bandhur ƒÅtma-ƒÅtmanas tasya yena ƒÅtmƒÅiva ƒÅtmana jitah,
AnƒÅtmanastu ≈õatrutve vartet ƒÅtmƒÅiva ≈õatruvat.

Symbolism: The mind and self are one‚Äôs friend when controlled, enemy when uncontrolled.

English: One who has conquered the self by the self has a friend in oneself; one who fails becomes an enemy to oneself.

Meaning: Self-mastery determines inner harmony or conflict.

Full Explanation: Krishna stresses that self-control is essential. A disciplined mind supports spiritual growth, whereas a restless or uncontrolled mind leads to inner strife.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.10

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö | ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É |
‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§®‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç ||

≈örƒ´-bhagavƒÅn uvƒÅca: Yogƒ´ yu√±jƒ´ta satata·πÅ mƒÅnasa·πÅ ≈õƒÅntamanƒÅ·∏•,
≈öarƒ´ra·πÅ yathƒÅ-≈õakti niyamya naitya-ƒÅtmanyeva va≈õa·πÅ nayet.

Symbolism: Moderation in lifestyle is essential for meditation and spiritual growth.

English: A yogi should practice constantly, with a tranquil mind, controlling the body according to one‚Äôs capacity, and keep the mind focused on the self.

Meaning: Discipline, moderation, and focus are key to meditation.

Full Explanation: Krishna advises that excessive indulgence or austerity is harmful. A yogi must maintain balance in eating, sleeping, and activities, while directing the mind steadily towards self-realization.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.16

‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§ö‡•à‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡§É |
‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ||

NƒÅtya-≈õnatastu yogo ‚Äôsti na chaikƒÅntam ana≈õnatah,
Na chƒÅtya-≈õƒ´to·π£·πáa sukha-du·∏•khe·π£u sama·∏• kartƒÅ.

Symbolism: Moderation is essential; extremes in eating, sleeping, or comfort hinder meditation.

English: Yoga is not for one who eats too much or too little, or who sleeps excessively or negligently; balance in all things is key.

Meaning: A yogi should maintain moderation in eating, sleeping, and daily activities.

Full Explanation: Krishna teaches that extremes are obstacles to meditation and spiritual progress. A balanced lifestyle is essential to control the mind and body effectively for yoga.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.17

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡§É |
‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ö ||

Yu√±jann eva yogam brahma·πáya-samƒÅhita·∏• sthira·∏•,
Mana·∏• sa·πÅyamya indriyƒÅ·πái mayi sarvƒÅ·πái karmƒÅ·πái cha.

Symbolism: Balanced meditation requires controlling the mind and senses while performing duties.

English: The yogi, established in Brahman, practices yoga, controlling the mind and senses, and dedicates all actions to Me.

Meaning: Integration of meditation and action, with focus and devotion.

Full Explanation: Krishna instructs that a true yogi maintains equilibrium: performs duties without attachment, controls the senses, and remains absorbed in the divine while practicing meditation.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.29

‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø |
‡§à‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡§É ||

Sarva-bh≈´ta-stham ƒÅtmaƒÅnam sarva-bh≈´tƒÅni cha ƒÅtmani,
ƒ™k·π£ate yoga-yukta-ƒÅtmƒÅ sarvatra sama-dar≈õinah.

Symbolism: A yogi sees the same self in all beings, fostering equality and compassion.

English: The yogi, united in yoga, sees the same self dwelling in all beings everywhere.

Meaning: Equality and compassion arise from recognizing the self in all.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that a realized yogi perceives the same divine essence in every creature, leading to detachment from discrimination and cultivating universal love.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.33

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö | ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç-‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ |
‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§É ||

≈örƒ´-bhagavƒÅn uvƒÅca: Yasya sarve samƒÅrambhƒÅ mad-bhƒÅvanƒÅ·πÅ tyaktvƒÅ,
Citte pratyeti niruddha·πÅ yoga·πÅ samƒÅcarata·∏•.

Symbolism: Devotion and focus on Krishna leads the yogi to mastery over mind and action.

English: The yogi who renounces all undertakings motivated by personal desires and dedicates all thoughts to Me attains steady yoga.

Meaning: Focusing the mind on Krishna while renouncing selfish desires leads to mastery in yoga.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes that detachment from personal motives and constant remembrance of the divine bring control over the mind and inner peace for the yogi.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.36

‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç |
‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç ||

Yatnena cittasya sthirasya yogino ‚Äôvasthitam,
Ni·π£kƒÅma·πÅ karma kuryƒÅd yathƒÅ yoga·πÅ samƒÅcaran.

Symbolism: The yogi should perform actions without desire for fruits, steadily and with focus.

English: The yogi with a steady mind performs actions without attachment, practicing yoga continuously.

Meaning: Detachment and focus are key to effective spiritual practice.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes that consistent, selfless action with mental stability is the hallmark of a yogi, leading to spiritual progress and inner peace.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.47

‡§Ø‡§É ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É |
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ö ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É ||

Ya·∏• yogƒ´ mad-bhakta·∏• sa me priya·∏•,
SarvathƒÅ priya·∏• cha sa yo·π£ita·∏•.

Symbolism: The yogi devoted to Krishna is always dear to Him, emphasizing devotion over ritual.

English: The yogi devoted to Me is always dear to Me in all respects.

Meaning: Devotion is the highest form of yoga and is pleasing to Krishna.

Full Explanation: Krishna assures that a yogi who surrenders with love and devotion transcends rituals and attains closeness to the divine.

Dhyana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 6.50

‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ß‡§®‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø |
‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó ‡§â‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ||

Yogastha·∏• kuru karmƒÅ·πái sa·πÖga·πÅ tyaktvƒÅ dhana√±jaya,
Siddhy-asiddhyo·∏• samo bh≈´tvƒÅ samatva·πÅ yoga ucyate.

Symbolism: Equanimity in success and failure while performing duty is true yoga.

English: O Dhananjaya, perform your duties while remaining steadfast in yoga, renouncing attachment, treating success and failure alike.

Meaning: True yoga is maintaining equanimity in all outcomes while performing one‚Äôs responsibilities.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that the yogi is not swayed by the dualities of life‚Äîsuccess and failure, pleasure and pain‚Äîbut performs duty with a balanced mind, which is the essence of yoga.

Jnana Vijnana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 7.3

‡§Ö‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§É |
‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏ ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡§∞‡§É ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§® ||

Adbhuta·πÅ parama·πÅ bhƒÅva·πÅ jƒÅnƒÅti yogino vidu·∏•,
Aha·πÅ bhƒÅvo BhagavƒÅn sa nƒÅtra para·∏• ka≈õcana.

Symbolism: Yogis recognize Krishna as the supreme, wonderful, and ultimate divine essence, beyond ordinary perception.

English: Those who are wise perceive the wondrous supreme state of the Lord. I am the divine essence, and there is no one higher than Me.

Meaning: Krishna is the ultimate reality; yogis understand His supreme and miraculous nature.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that the enlightened see His divine form in all things and recognize Him as the ultimate cause of everything, beyond any other existence.

Jnana Vijnana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 7.7

‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§§‡•á |
‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á ||

Matta·∏• paratara·πÅ nƒÅnyat ki√±ca jayate,
Mayi sarva·πÅ pravartate.

Symbolism: Krishna is the ultimate cause; everything originates and functions in Him.

English: There is nothing higher than Me. Everything emanates from Me and exists because of Me.

Meaning: Krishna is the source of all creation; nothing exists beyond Him.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes His supremacy: all beings and matter emerge from Him, are sustained by Him, and ultimately dissolve into Him, establishing Him as the ultimate reality.

Jnana Vijnana Yoga

‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á |
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ||

Iti matvƒÅ bhajante mƒÅ·πÅ budhƒÅ bhƒÅva-samanvitƒÅ·∏•.

Symbolism: Krishna is the principal source of everything; wise devotees recognize and worship Him with understanding.

English: I am the source of all; everything proceeds from Me. Wise ones, understanding this, worship Me with devotion.

Meaning: Recognizing Krishna as the prime cause, enlightened devotees dedicate themselves to Him.

Full Explanation: Krishna declares that all creation originates from Him, and the intelligent, realizing this truth, engage in devotional worship, connecting intellect with love and understanding.

‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ω‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É ||

Dravya-j√±ƒÅnƒ´ cha bhƒÅva-j√±ƒÅnƒ´ cha bh≈´yo bh≈´yo mƒÅm upƒÅsate,
J√±ƒÅna-v·πõddho ‚ÄôthavƒÅ bhaktyƒÅ mƒÅm eti pa·πá·∏çita·∏• puru·π£a·∏•.

Symbolism: Devotees may worship Krishna with knowledge of the material or the divine essence; the wise approach Him with devotion.

English: Some worship Me with knowledge of the material world, some with knowledge of My divine essence. The wise one, with knowledge or devotion, comes to Me.

Meaning: Both intellectual understanding and loving devotion lead to connection with Krishna.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that devotees have different approaches‚Äîsome study the material and divine aspects, some focus on pure devotion‚Äîbut all wise people ultimately reach Him.

Jnana Vijnana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 7.14

‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å |
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ||

Man-manƒÅ bhava mad-bhakto mad-yƒÅjƒ´ mƒÅ·πÅ namaskuru,
MƒÅm eva e·π£yasi satya·πÅ te pratijƒÅne priyo ‚Äôsi me.

Symbolism: Constant remembrance, devotion, and worship bring the devotee closer to Krishna.

English: Fix your mind on Me, be devoted, offer Me worship, and bow to Me. I promise you will come to Me. You are dear to Me.

Meaning: Sincere devotion and remembrance of Krishna ensure closeness and love from Him.

Full Explanation: Krishna assures that those who dedicate their mind, actions, and worship to Him with faith and devotion will attain Him and remain beloved in His eyes.

Jnana Vijnana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 7.15

‡§Ö‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç |
‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ||

A-j√±ƒÅna·πÅ chƒÅ-vidyƒÅna·πÅ mat-prasƒÅdƒÅt param,
Eva·πÅ vidvƒÅn bhajate mƒÅm abhyas≈´yam ƒÅsakta·∏•.

Symbolism: Most people are deluded by ignorance, but grace and knowledge remove obstacles for the devotee.

English: Due to ignorance, most people are deluded, but by My grace, the wise devotee attains knowledge and devotion, free from envy.

Meaning: Krishna‚Äôs grace illuminates the mind, enabling sincere devotion and wisdom.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that ignorance traps most beings in material illusion. However, those who are wise and devoted, by His mercy, overcome jealousy and see the truth.

Bhagavad Gita 7.16

‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® |
‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠ ||

Chatur-vidhƒÅ bhajante mƒÅ·πÅ janƒÅ·∏• su-k·πõtino ‚Äôrjuna,
ƒÄrto jij√±ƒÅsur arthƒÅrthƒ´ j√±ƒÅnƒ´ cha bharatar·π£abha.

Symbolism: Four types of virtuous people approach Krishna: distressed, seekers of knowledge, seekers of wealth, and wise devotees.

English: O Arjuna, four types of devotees worship Me: those in distress, seekers of knowledge, seekers of material gain, and the wise.

Meaning: People approach Krishna with different motivations, yet all sincere devotion is valued.

Full Explanation: Krishna categorizes His devotees into four types: those suffering in life (ƒÅrta), those seeking spiritual knowledge (jij√±ƒÅsu), those seeking material wealth (arthƒÅrthƒ´), and the wise (j√±ƒÅnƒ´). All who sincerely worship Him are blessed.

Jnana Vijnana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 7.17

‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§ó‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç |
‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§®‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ||

Te·π£ƒÅm aha·πÅ samuddhartƒÅ m·πõtyu-sa·πÅsƒÅra-sƒÅgarƒÅt,
BhavƒÅmi na cirƒÅt pƒÅrtha mayyƒÅve≈õita-cetasƒÅm.

Symbolism: Krishna rescues devotees from the ocean of material existence, especially those devoted to Him with focused mind.

English: I deliver those devotees who are devoted to Me with steadfast mind from the ocean of birth and death; I do not delay.

Meaning: Krishna promptly rescues those who sincerely dedicate themselves to Him.

Full Explanation: Krishna assures Arjuna that devotees who focus their mind on Him and surrender are immediately freed from the cycle of material existence, showing His grace and protective nature.

Akshara Brahma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 8.3

‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç |
‡§Ø ‡§è‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ||

Avyakto ‚Äôk·π£ara ity ukto brahma·πáo ‚Äôparam matam,
Ya ena·πÅ vetti hantƒÅra·πÅ ya≈õ caina·πÅ manyate m·πõtam.

Symbolism: The imperishable Brahman is beyond material perception; the ignorant mistake it for the mortal.

English: The Supreme Being is imperishable and beyond the material world. Those who recognize this attain Him; the ignorant consider Him as mortal.

Meaning: Understanding Brahman‚Äôs imperishable nature is key to liberation.

Full Explanation: Krishna teaches that Brahman is eternal and unaffected by birth or death. Only those who know this truth are liberated, while the ignorant are trapped in material misconceptions.

Akshara Brahma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 8.5

‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø |
‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§É ||

Ya·∏• prayƒÅti sa mad-bhƒÅva·πÅ yƒÅti nƒÅstya-tra san≈õaya·∏•.

Symbolism: Remembering Krishna at the time of death leads the soul to Him, removing all doubt.

English: Whoever remembers Me at the time of death, thinking of My supreme nature, attains Me without doubt.

Meaning: Focused remembrance of Krishna at death ensures liberation.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes the power of devotion and remembrance at the final moment. The mind absorbed in Him transcends birth and death and reaches the Supreme.

Akshara Brahma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 8.6

‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç |
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§∂‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç ||

Ya·πÅ ya·πÅ vai karmƒÅ·πái sa·πÖga·πÅ tyaktvƒÅ mƒÅ·πÅ samƒÅcaran,
An≈õamanto ‚Äôpi mƒÅ·πÅ tva·πÅ yƒÅnty eva·πÅ uttamƒÅ·πÅ gatim.

Symbolism: Actions performed without attachment, dedicated to Krishna, lead the soul to the supreme destination.

English: Whatever actions one performs without attachment, dedicating them to Me, even at death, leads to the supreme goal.

Meaning: Detached, devotional action is the path to liberation.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes karma without attachment. Even if one dies while performing duties devoted to Him, the soul attains liberation, highlighting the power of selfless action.

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö |
‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§É ||

Mayy arpita-manobuddhir mƒÅm eva e·π£yasi san≈õaya·∏•.

Symbolism: Constant remembrance and devotion to Krishna in all times lead to Him without doubt.

English: Therefore, at all times, remember Me, fight your duties with mind and intellect dedicated to Me; doubtlessly you will reach Me.

Meaning: Continuous devotion and focused action ensure union with Krishna.

Full Explanation: Krishna instructs that unwavering remembrance and dedication in every activity of life guide the soul to Him, emphasizing devotion as the ultimate path.

Akshara Brahma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 8.10

‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•å ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§ ‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§Æ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á |
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ||

Agneau cha sapta vairi·πáƒÅ yama iva chƒÅbhidhƒ´yate,
Sarpebhyo naraka≈õchaiva yamasyaiva nigamyate.

Symbolism: The danger of material entanglements is described, emphasizing that devotion leads one beyond worldly punishments.

English: Just as the seven flames of fire can burn, and Yama punishes wrongdoers, similarly worldly dangers cannot harm the soul devoted to Me.

Meaning: Devotion to Krishna protects the soul from all material dangers and karmic reactions.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that worldly punishments, death, and even hellish experiences cannot touch the devoted soul, showing the supreme protection granted to sincere devotees.

Akshara Brahma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 8.13

‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ó‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§ø ‡§®‡§É |
‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§® ‡§π‡§ø ‡§®‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ||

Kasmin sthi cha mamƒÅtmƒÅ gata·∏• pramu√±jate hi na·∏•,
YadƒÅ hi na hi no hi svo hi prapadyate.

Symbolism: Consistently remembering the Supreme ensures the soul merges with the imperishable Brahman.

English: By consistently focusing on Me, the soul departs and merges into the imperishable Brahman.

Meaning: Continuous remembrance of Krishna leads to liberation and merging with the eternal.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes the importance of constant devotion and meditation to reach the imperishable Brahman, transcending birth and death.

Akshara Brahma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 8.16

‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç |
‡§Ø ‡§è‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ||

Avyakto ‚Äôk·π£ara ity ukto brahma·πáo ‚Äôparam matam,
Ya ena·πÅ vetti hantƒÅra·πÅ ya≈õ caina·πÅ manyate m·πõtam.

Symbolism: Brahman is imperishable, while the material world is transient; recognizing this leads to liberation.

English: The Supreme Brahman is imperishable; those who know this reach liberation, while the ignorant consider it mortal.

Meaning: Understanding the eternal nature of Brahman is key to freedom from the cycle of birth and death.

Full Explanation: Krishna reiterates that Brahman is eternal and beyond decay, whereas the material world is temporary. Realizing this truth leads the soul to liberation.

‡∞Ö‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞•‡∞Ç: ‡∞¨‡±ç‡∞∞‡∞π‡±ç‡∞Æ ‡∞Ø‡±ä‡∞ï‡±ç‡∞ï ‡∞∂‡∞æ‡∞∂‡±ç‡∞µ‡∞§ ‡∞∏‡±ç‡∞µ‡∞≠‡∞æ‡∞µ‡∞æ‡∞®‡±ç‡∞®‡∞ø ‡∞Ö‡∞∞‡±ç‡∞•‡∞Ç ‡∞ö‡±á‡∞∏‡±Å‡∞ï‡±ã‡∞µ‡∞°‡∞Ç ‡∞ú‡∞®‡∞®‡∞Ç ‡∞Æ‡∞∞‡∞ø‡∞Ø‡±Å ‡∞Æ‡±É‡∞§‡∞ø‡∞®‡∞ø ‡∞Ö‡∞ß‡∞ø‡∞ó‡∞Æ‡∞ø‡∞Ç‡∞ö‡∞°‡∞æ‡∞®‡∞ø‡∞ï‡∞ø ‡∞Æ‡±Å‡∞ñ‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞Æ‡±à‡∞®‡∞¶‡∞ø.

‡∞µ‡∞ø‡∞µ‡∞∞‡∞£: ‡∞ï‡±É‡∞∑‡±ç‡∞£‡±Å‡∞°‡±Å ‡∞Æ‡∞∞‡∞≤ ‡∞µ‡∞ø‡∞µ‡∞∞‡∞ø‡∞∏‡±ç‡∞§‡±Å‡∞®‡±ç‡∞®‡∞æ‡∞∞‡±Å, ‡∞¨‡±ç‡∞∞‡∞π‡±ç‡∞Æ ‡∞∂‡∞æ‡∞∂‡±ç‡∞µ‡∞§‡∞Æ‡±à‡∞®‡∞¶‡∞ø ‡∞Æ‡∞∞‡∞ø‡∞Ø‡±Å ‡∞Ö‡∞µ‡∞ø‡∞®‡∞æ‡∞∂‡±Ä; ‡∞≠‡±å‡∞§‡∞ø‡∞ï ‡∞™‡±ç‡∞∞‡∞™‡∞Ç‡∞ö‡∞Ç ‡∞§‡∞æ‡∞§‡±ç‡∞ï‡∞æ‡∞≤‡∞ø‡∞ï‡∞Ç. ‡∞à ‡∞∏‡∞§‡±ç‡∞Ø‡∞æ‡∞®‡±ç‡∞®‡∞ø ‡∞§‡±Ü‡∞≤‡±Å‡∞∏‡±Å‡∞ï‡±ã‡∞µ‡∞°‡∞Ç ‡∞¶‡±ç‡∞µ‡∞æ‡∞∞‡∞æ ‡∞Ü‡∞§‡±ç‡∞Æ ‡∞µ‡∞ø‡∞Æ‡±Å‡∞ï‡±ç‡∞§‡∞ø ‡∞™‡±ä‡∞Ç‡∞¶‡±Å‡∞§‡±Å‡∞Ç‡∞¶‡∞ø.

Akshara Brahma Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 8.17

‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§É |
‡§Ö‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§ ||

Antavanta ime dehƒÅ nityasyoktƒÅ·∏• ≈õarƒ´ri·πáa·∏•,
AnƒÅ≈õino ‚Äôprameyasya tasmƒÅd yudhyasva bhƒÅrata.

Symbolism: The body is temporary, but the soul is eternal and indestructible; understanding this helps one act without fear.

English: These bodies are temporary, O Bharata, but the soul is eternal and indestructible; therefore fight without fear.

Meaning: Understanding the soul‚Äôs immortality removes fear in battle and in life.

Full Explanation: Krishna advises Arjuna that the physical body is perishable, but the soul is eternal. Realizing this, one can perform duties courageously, knowing the soul remains unharmed.

Raja Vidya Raja Guhya Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 9.4

‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á |
‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ ||

Mayy eva·πÅ≈õo ‚Äôk·πõta·∏• sarva·∏• pralaya·πÅ tasyopajƒÅyate,
Sattvam ƒÅtmam ƒÅyayƒÅ yato jagad avyakta·πÅ param.

Symbolism: Everything emanates from the Supreme; the material world is temporary while the soul is eternal.

English: All beings originate from Me; when they dissolve, they return to Me. The material world is temporary, and the soul is My eternal fragment.

Meaning: Krishna explains the eternal nature of the soul and the temporary nature of the material world.

Full Explanation: The Supreme Being creates all manifestations. Everything merges back into Him at dissolution, emphasizing the imperishable essence of the soul versus the transient material world.

Raja Vidya Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 9.5

‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§® ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§§‡§É |
‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡•ç ||

Bh≈´tabhƒÅvana bhavƒÅbh≈´tabhyo janto·∏• pitara·πÅ mƒÅ·πÅ pra·πáata·∏•,
Katha·πÅ bh≈´tƒÅbhimƒÅna·πÅ dhƒÅrayan pa≈õyƒÅmi jagat.

Symbolism: Krishna pervades all beings but remains independent; the world is His creation, yet He transcends it.

English: Though I am the father of all beings and pervade them, I remain independent. Yet the world appears sustained by Me.

Meaning: Krishna exists within all beings but is beyond dependence.

Full Explanation: This verse emphasizes Krishna‚Äôs transcendental position: He is immanent in all beings but also supremely independent, highlighting the balance between His immanence and transcendence.

Raja Vidya Raja Guhya Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 9.7

‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ||

Symbolism: Devotion to the imperishable Supreme grants liberation and protection.

English: Those who worship the imperishable, unmanifest, eternal Supreme are freed from all sins.

Meaning: Devotion to the eternal Supreme purifies and liberates the soul.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes that devotion to Him, the eternal and imperishable Brahman, protects one from all karmic reactions and leads to liberation.

Raja Vidya Raja Guhya Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 9.13

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§É |
‡§∏ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç ||

Karma·πáyakarma ya·∏• pa≈õyed akarma·πái cha karma ya·∏•,
Sa buddhimƒÅn manu·π£ye·π£u sa yukta·∏• k·πõtsnakarmak·πõt.

Symbolism: The wise see action and inaction, performing all duties without attachment.

English: One who sees inaction in action and action in inaction is wise. Such a person is disciplined and performs all duties efficiently.

Meaning: True wisdom lies in performing duties without attachment while recognizing the ultimate reality.

Full Explanation: Krishna teaches that a person who acts without ego, seeing the transient nature of actions and results, achieves harmony and efficiency in life.

Raja Vidya Raja Guhya Yoga

Symbolism: Krishna promises protection and provision to those who are devoted exclusively to Him.

English: Those who worship Me with exclusive devotion, constantly meditating on Me, I provide them with all their needs and protect them.

Meaning: Krishna assures the devotees of complete care and sustenance.

Full Explanation: Devotion to Krishna guarantees spiritual and material security, showing that surrender and love for the divine are rewarded.

Patram pu·π£pam phalam toya·πÅ yo me bhakty upah·πõtam,
Tad aha·πÅ bhakty upah·πõtam a≈õnƒÅmi prayatƒÅtmanah.

Symbolism: Even simple offerings made with devotion are accepted by Krishna.

English: Whatever leaf, flower, fruit, or water is offered to Me with devotion, I accept it from the pure-hearted devotee.

Meaning: Sincere offerings, no matter how small, are cherished by Krishna.

Full Explanation: The act of giving with devotion is more important than the material value of the offering. Krishna honors the love behind the offering.

Raja Vidya Raja Guhya Yoga

‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§π‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø ‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç |
‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ||

English: Whatever you do, eat, offer, or practice in austerity, dedicate it to Me, O Arjuna.

Symbolism: Krishna is the source of all creation, and everything operates under His guidance.

Full Explanation: Krishna reveals His role as the ultimate source behind all natural processes. Though creation seems independent, it is governed by His divine energy.

Full Explanation: Understanding Krishna as the ultimate source motivates enlightened beings to offer their actions and hearts entirely to Him, cultivating spiritual wisdom.

‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§°‡§æ‡§ï‡•á‡§∂ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É |
‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ö ||

Aha·πÅ ƒÅtmƒÅ gu·∏çƒÅke≈õa sarvabh≈´tƒÅ≈õayasthita·∏•,
Aham ƒÅdi≈õ ca madhya·πÅ ca bh≈´tƒÅnƒÅm anta eva ca.

Symbolism: Krishna is the inner Self, the beginning, middle, and end of all beings.

English: I am the Self, O Arjuna, dwelling in the hearts of all beings. I am the beginning, middle, and end of all creatures.

Meaning: Krishna pervades all life as the eternal Self and essence of existence.

Full Explanation: This verse shows that Krishna is both immanent and transcendent, present in all beings as their inner consciousness and as the source and ultimate destination of everything.

‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡§æ |

Mayi sarvƒÅ·πái karmƒÅ·πái sannyasyƒÅdhyƒÅtma-cetasƒÅ,

Symbolism: Offering all actions to Krishna with devotion ensures spiritual liberation.

English: Devotees dedicate all their actions to Me, with minds focused on the self and devotion, remaining unattached.

Full Explanation: By performing all duties as offerings to Krishna, one achieves spiritual growth while remaining detached from outcomes, reflecting the essence of Karma Yoga.

Symbolism: Knowledge, wisdom, and devotion to Krishna together lead to spiritual perfection.

English: O Arjuna, this knowledge I have explained, together with wisdom, dedicated to Me by devoted souls, leads to supreme understanding.

Vibhuti Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 10.41

‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§™‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§®‡•á‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ã‡§™‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§æ |
‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ||

YathƒÅ dƒ´po nivƒÅtastho ne·πÖgate sopamƒÅ sm·πõtƒÅ,
Yogino yatacittƒÅtmƒÅ nitya·πÅ yoga-yukto bhavati.

Symbolism: The soul devoted to Krishna shines with steady wisdom, like a lamp in still air, symbolizing spiritual illumination and focus.

English: Just as a lamp in a windless place burns steadily, a yogi with controlled mind remains focused on Me eternally.

Meaning: Devotion and yoga bring inner steadiness and spiritual enlightenment.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that a devotee, like a lamp in calm air, maintains unwavering focus and illumination through yoga and devotion. Such focus allows the soul to connect deeply with the divine.

Vishwaroopa Darshana Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 11.33

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö | ‡§π‡•á ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£, ‡§π‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞, ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™ ‡§¶‡•á‡§ñ‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç‡§™ ‡§∞‡§π‡§æ ‡§π‡•à |

Mujhe yoddhƒÅ bankar yuddha karne kƒÅ sƒÅhas do.

Symbolism: Arjuna acknowledges fear and seeks divine courage to act.

English: Arjuna says: O Krishna, seeing this terrifying form, my mind trembles. Give me the courage to fight.

Meaning: Human fear is natural even for the righteous; divine guidance strengthens courage.

Full Explanation: Arjuna recognizes his fear before the overwhelming cosmic form and prays to Krishna for fortitude to fulfill his dharma in battle.

Bhakti Yoga

‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§É |

Symbolism: Arjuna asks Krishna which form of worship (personal God or formless) is superior, showing the path of devotion.

Full Explanation: Arjuna wants to know whether devotion to a personal form or formless aspect of God leads to liberation and closeness to Krishna.

Symbolism: Always think of Krishna, dedicate actions to Him, and surrender to Him fully.

English: Krishna says: Fix your mind on Me, be devoted, offer all actions to Me, bow to Me. You will come to Me without doubt.

Bhakti Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 12.14

‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É ‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•É‡§¢‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡§É |
‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É ||

Santu·π£·π≠a·∏• satata·πÅ yogƒ´ yatƒÅtmƒÅ d·πõ·∏çhani≈õcaya·∏•,
Mayyarpita-manobuddhir yo mad-bhakta·∏• sa me priya·∏•.

Symbolism: The devotee is content, self-controlled, steady, and mind and intellect dedicated to Krishna.

English: Krishna says: The devotee who is satisfied, disciplined, firm, and dedicates mind and intellect to Me is dear to Me.

Meaning: Spiritual contentment and dedication attract divine grace.

Full Explanation: The qualities of a steady, dedicated, and content devotee make them close to God and ensure spiritual progress.

Bhakti Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 12.15

‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§É |
‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡§Ø‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É ||

YasmƒÅn nodvijate loko lokƒÅn nodvijate cha ya·∏•,
Har·π£ƒÅmar·π£a-bhayo-dvegair mukto ya·∏• sa cha me priya·∏•.

Symbolism: The devotee who is peaceful, undisturbed by the world, and free from joy, envy, fear, or hatred is dear to Krishna.

English: Krishna says: One who is not agitated by the world and does not agitate others, free from attachment, fear, and anger, is dear to Me.

Meaning: Equanimity, self-control, and freedom from negative emotions are qualities of a beloved devotee.

Full Explanation: Such a devotee maintains calmness in all circumstances and treats others with kindness, reflecting spiritual maturity and closeness to Krishna.

Bhakti Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 12.16

‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡§É |
‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§≤‡§É ||

SƒÅdhu-ramƒ´cƒ´no bh≈´tvƒÅ d·πõ·π£·π≠avya·∏• sadƒÅ hi sa·∏•,
Sarvebhyo hi priya·∏• syƒÅn nodvijate cha mahƒÅbala·∏•.

Symbolism: A devotee with virtue and balanced behavior, loved by all and unshaken even by the strongest forces.

English: The virtuous devotee is always to be observed; loved by all, unshaken by difficulties and challenges.

Meaning: Moral virtue and calmness make the devotee universally dear and spiritually strong.

Full Explanation: Such a devotee does not create disturbance, remains steady in adversity, and inspires respect and affection in all beings.

Bhakti Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 12.19

‡§è‡§∑‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§®‡•à‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø |
‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•á ||

E·π£ƒÅ brƒÅhmƒ´ sthiti pƒÅrtha nainƒÅ·πÅ prƒÅpya vina≈õyati,

Symbolism: The devotee who attains this spiritual state is liberated and reaches Krishna directly.

English: Krishna says: The devotee who attains this state is never lost; they reach Me and enjoy eternal union.

Meaning: Spiritual attainment through devotion leads to immortality and closeness to God.

Full Explanation: By cultivating devotion and virtuous conduct, the soul becomes free from material entanglements and achieves eternal connection with Krishna.

Bhakti Yoga

Symbolism: Those who act ignorantly and are not devoted suffer; devotion brings auspiciousness and spiritual progress.

English: Krishna says: One who acts ignorantly and without devotion is lost; devotion leads to auspiciousness and closeness to Me.

Full Explanation: Devotion to Krishna is the safeguard against spiritual ignorance and brings divine guidance and eternal benefit.

Kshetra Kshetrajna Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 13.1

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö | ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á |
‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§É ||

≈örƒ´-BhagavƒÅn uvƒÅca: Ida·πÅ ≈õarƒ´ra·πÅ kaunteya k·π£etram ity abhidhƒ´yate,
Etad yo vetti ta·πÅ prƒÅhu·∏• k·π£etraj√±a iti tad-vidah.

Symbolism: Krishna defines the body as the ‚Äúfield‚Äù and the knower of the field as the soul.

English: Krishna says: O son of Kunti, this body is called the field, and one who knows it is called the knower of the field.

Meaning: The physical body is temporary, while the soul observes and experiences it.

Full Explanation: This verse introduces the concept of the body (Kshetra) and soul (Kshetragna), forming the foundation of spiritual knowledge.

Kshetra Kshetrajna Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 13.2

‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§É |

Symbolism: Understanding the field and knower purifies the soul through knowledge and action.

English: The wise declare that knowledge of the field and its knower is the path to self-purification through action and wisdom.

Meaning: Spiritual knowledge combined with right action purifies the soul.

Full Explanation: By understanding both the body and the soul, one attains clarity, self-realization, and progress in yoga.

Kshetra Kshetrajna Vibhaga Yoga

Symbolism: Knowing the soul as the doer within the body leads to true happiness.

English: Krishna says: One who understands Me as the ultimate doer, while recognizing the body as the instrument, is a yogi and is truly happy.

Meaning: Awareness of the soul as the true actor brings joy and equanimity.

Full Explanation: This verse emphasizes that self-realization and understanding the distinction between body and soul is the path to happiness and liberation.

Symbolism: Describes qualities like humility, non-violence, self-control, and forgiveness as leading to liberation.

English: Krishna describes the virtues and knowledge that lead the soul toward liberation.

Symbolism: Krishna emphasizes that selfless action and knowledge lead to liberation, not material desires.

English: Krishna says: I do not desire kingdoms, heaven, or rebirth; I attain liberation through knowledge and selfless action.

Meaning: Spiritual progress is the true aim, beyond worldly desires.

Full Explanation: Krishna sets the example of detachment, showing that liberation comes from wisdom, virtue, and devotion.

‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§® ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ |
‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ||

Yac cƒÅnyad veda na veda tad veditavya·πÅ karma,
Arjuna sama·∏• sarvatra sama·∏• sarve·π£u kƒÅle·π£u.

Symbolism: Knowledge of what is to be known and performing duties with equanimity in all times leads to wisdom.

English: A yogi who is balanced in all activities and aware of what needs to be known attains perfection.

Meaning: Equanimity and discernment in action cultivate spiritual wisdom.

Full Explanation: Recognizing knowledge and performing duties without attachment, in all circumstances, leads to liberation and union with the divine.

Kshetra-Kshetragna Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 13.27-13.33

‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É |
‡§∏ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•à‡§É ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ||

Ya·∏• sarvatr anabhisneha·∏• p·πõcchati yoga-yukta·∏•,
Sa eva mucyate sarva-pƒÅpai·∏• yogino 'tƒ´mukta·∏•.

Symbolism: A yogi free from attachment, who constantly seeks Krishna, is liberated from all sins.

English: The yogi, detached from worldly desires and devoted to Krishna, is freed from all sins.

Meaning: Detachment and devotion lead to liberation.

Full Explanation: Krishna explains that the spiritually enlightened person who maintains equanimity, seeks divine knowledge, and renounces attachment attains ultimate freedom.

Gunatraya Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 14.4

‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§É |
‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡§ß‡•ç‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§É ||

Sattva·πÅ rajas tama iti gu·πáƒÅ·∏• prak·πõti-sambhavƒÅ·∏•,
Nibadhnanti mahƒÅ-bƒÅho deha·πÅ karmƒÅ·πái sarva≈õa·∏•.

Symbolism: All material actions and experiences are bound by the three gunas (Sattva, Rajas, Tamas).

English: Krishna explains that the three gunas‚ÄîSattva, Rajas, Tamas‚Äîbind all beings to actions and the body.

Meaning: Material nature governs all activities through the gunas.

Full Explanation: Understanding that these qualities pervade everything helps the yogi act without attachment and aim for liberation.

Gunatraya Vibhaga Yoga

‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É |

Symbolism: Each guna produces its characteristic effect‚ÄîSattva brings happiness, Rajas creates activity, Tamas leads to ignorance.

English: Krishna explains how each guna produces distinct tendencies in beings.

Meaning: Sattva = harmony, Rajas = passion, Tamas = ignorance.

Full Explanation: Understanding guna effects helps the yogi overcome attachments and act wisely.

Gunatraya Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 14.7

‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§Æ |
‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ||

Sattva·πÅ rajas tama iti prak·πõti·πÅ viddhi mama,
BhavƒÅbhava-vinirmukta·πÅ mama deham ƒÅsthita·πÅ.

Symbolism: The body is influenced by gunas, but the soul remains free from birth and death.

English: The soul resides in the body influenced by the gunas but remains untouched by birth and death.

Meaning: The soul is eternal; the body is temporary and influenced by material nature.

Full Explanation: Recognizing this distinction helps the yogi act without attachment and focus on spiritual liberation.

Gunatraya Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 14.13

‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡•ã ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Æ |
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§§‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ||

Sattva·πÅ sukham ity u cha j√±ƒÅna·πÅ tejo gata·πÅ mama,
RƒÅjasam cha lam kƒÅma·πÅ ity eva tama·∏• prajƒÅyate.

Symbolism: Sattva brings happiness and knowledge; Rajas produces desire and action; Tamas leads to ignorance.

English: Krishna explains the characteristic effects of the three gunas on beings.

Meaning: Sattva = knowledge & happiness, Rajas = desire & restlessness, Tamas = ignorance & inertia.

Full Explanation: Recognizing how gunas influence mind and behavior helps the aspirant manage desires and cultivate wisdom.

Symbolism: Sattva is pure and enlightened, Rajas is driven by desire, Tamas is obstructive and deluded.

English: Characteristics of the three gunas: Sattva is constructive, Rajas is desire-driven, Tamas is obstructive.

Meaning: Awareness of guna nature helps control actions and mind.

Full Explanation: Recognizing these tendencies aids the yogi in choosing sattvic actions and transcending rajas and tamas.

RƒÅjas tu kƒÅma-v·πõttir malino dvaya·πÅ tamasi.

Symbolism: Sattva produces stable happiness, Rajas is desire-driven, Tamas is heavy and deluded.

English: Sattva gives pure happiness, Rajas causes restless desire, Tamas is heavy and deluded.

Meaning: Observing the gunas helps in self-control and spiritual practice.

Full Explanation: Identifying these qualities in oneself enables the yogi to cultivate Sattva and transcend Rajas and Tamas.

‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡•á |

Symbolism: Unwavering devotion lifts the devotee beyond the three gu·πáas into the Brahman state.

English: One who serves Me with undeviating bhakti-yoga transcends these gu·πáas and becomes fit for realization of Brahman.

Meaning: Steady devotion is the direct path to rise above sattva, rajas, and tamas.

Full Explanation: The verse teaches that consistent, exclusive devotion purifies the mind so fully that the binding qualities of nature no longer affect the devotee, who abides in the Brahman-conscious state.

Gunatraya Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 14.27

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§π‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö |
‡§∂‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ||

Brahma·πáo hi prati·π£·π≠hƒÅham am·πõtasyƒÅvyayasya ca,
≈öƒÅ≈õvatasya ca dharmasya sukhasyaikƒÅntikasya ca.

Symbolism: Krishna is the foundation of Brahman, the source of immortality, eternal dharma, and supreme bliss.

English: For I am the basis of the imperishable Brahman, of immortality, of the eternal dharma, and of unending bliss.

Meaning: The personal Lord underlies and supports impersonal Brahman.

Full Explanation: This clarifies the relationship between Krishna (the Supreme Person) and Brahman (the impersonal absolute): devotion to Krishna grants access to Brahman, eternal dharma, and supreme happiness.

Purushottama Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 15.1

‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§® ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§´‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§É |
‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ||

Udyame ‚Äôsmin punastu karma·πáƒÅ·πÅ phalƒÅnƒÅ·πÅ vairi·πáa·∏•,
Sukha·πÅ du·∏•kha·πÅ cha ye vartante tƒÅni tu karma·πái sthitƒÅ·∏•.

Symbolism: Introduces the supreme eternal banyan tree and the perishable-material world vs. imperishable-soul distinction.

English: Krishna describes the supreme eternal banyan tree, its roots upward and branches downward. The material world is temporary, while the soul is eternal.

Meaning: Understanding the impermanent and permanent helps distinguish body from soul.

Full Explanation: The perishable nature of the world and the eternal soul‚Äôs position are symbolized by the tree. One should aim to understand the spiritual essence and rise above material bondage.

Purushottama Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 15.7

‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ã ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§É |
‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡§∑‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡§ø ||

Mamaiva·πÅ≈õo jƒ´valoke jƒ´vabh≈´ta·∏• sanƒÅtana·∏•,

Symbolism: Krishna is the Supreme Lord; all living beings are part of His eternal energy, and He sustains mind and senses.

English: Krishna explains that all souls are part of His eternal energy, and the mind and senses are under His guidance.

Meaning: The living being is a fragment of the Supreme, eternal in nature.

Full Explanation: Understanding our eternal connection to Krishna helps us see ourselves as part of His divine energy and motivates surrender and devotion.

Meaning: Krishna pervades all beings and is the source of all knowledge.

Full Explanation: Recognition of Krishna as the supreme consciousness leads to spiritual insight and liberation.

Purushottama Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 15.16

‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•å ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•å ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ö |
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•Ä ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§ø‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å ||

DvƒÅvimau puru·π£au loke k·π£ara≈õcƒÅk·π£ara eva ca,

Symbolism: Two kinds of beings exist‚Äîthe perishable (body) and imperishable (soul).

English: In this world, there are two kinds of beings: the perishable, which inhabits the body, and the imperishable.

Meaning: The body is transient; the soul is eternal.

Full Explanation: Recognizing the distinction between the impermanent body and eternal soul is essential for spiritual understanding and detachment.

‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§™ ‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ||

≈örƒ´ BhagavƒÅn uvƒÅca:
Abhaya·πÅ sattva-sa·πÅ≈õuddhir j√±ƒÅna-yoga-vyavasthiti·∏•,
DƒÅna·πÅ dama≈õ ca yaj√±a≈õ ca svƒÅdhyƒÅyas tapa ƒÅrjavam.

Symbolism: Krishna begins describing the divine qualities, starting with fearlessness, purity, self-control, charity, and truthfulness.

English: The Blessed Lord said: Fearlessness, purity of heart, steadfastness in knowledge and yoga, charity, self-restraint, sacrifice, study of the scriptures, austerity, and honesty.

Meaning: These are the divine virtues that purify a person and lead towards liberation.

Full Explanation: Krishna begins listing the daivi-sampatti (divine qualities). Such traits elevate the soul and align it with dharma, helping in spiritual progress.

Daivasura Sampad Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 16.2

‡§Ö‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§É ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡•à‡§∂‡•Å‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç |

Symbolism: Non-violence, truth, forgiveness, peace, compassion, and humility are highlighted as divine virtues.

English: Non-violence, truthfulness, absence of anger, renunciation, tranquility, absence of fault-finding, compassion towards all beings, absence of greed, gentleness, modesty, and steadiness.

Meaning: These qualities foster harmony and uplift the soul.

Full Explanation: This verse elaborates on virtues like forgiveness, peace, and compassion that remove hatred and strengthen spiritual discipline.

Daivasura Sampad Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 16.3

‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•å‡§ö‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§æ |
‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§ ||

Teja·∏• k·π£amƒÅ dh·πõti·∏• ≈õaucam adroho nƒÅtimƒÅnitƒÅ,
Bhavanti sampada·πÅ daivƒ´m abhijƒÅtasya BhƒÅrata.

Symbolism: Strength, forgiveness, purity, humility, and freedom from hatred belong to the divine nature.

English: Vigor, forgiveness, fortitude, purity, absence of hatred, and freedom from pride ‚Äî these are the divine endowments, O Bharata.

Meaning: These qualities shape the character of the spiritually advanced soul.

Full Explanation: Krishna emphasizes virtues like patience and humility, which make one divine in nature. They stand in contrast to arrogance and hatred.

Daivasura Sampad Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 16.4

‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•ã ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§ö |
‡§Ö‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç ||

Dambho darpo‚ÄôbhimƒÅna≈õ ca krodha·∏• pƒÅru·π£yam eva ca,
Aj√±ƒÅna·πÅ cƒÅbhijƒÅtasya PƒÅrtha sampadƒÅm ƒÅsurƒ´m.

Symbolism: Hypocrisy, arrogance, pride, anger, harshness, and ignorance are marks of demonic nature.

English: O Partha, hypocrisy, arrogance, pride, anger, harshness, and ignorance are the qualities of those born with demoniac nature.

Meaning: These are destructive traits that bind the soul to suffering.

Full Explanation: Krishna contrasts asuric qualities with daivic ones. Such negative qualities obstruct spiritual growth and lead towards bondage and downfall.

Daivasura Sampad Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 16.5

‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§§‡§æ |
‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ ||

Daivƒ´ sampadvimok·π£ƒÅya nibandhƒÅyƒÅsurƒ´ matƒÅ,
MƒÅ ≈õucha·∏• sampada·πÅ daivƒ´m abhijƒÅto ‚Äôsi PƒÅ·πá·∏çava.

Symbolism: Divine qualities lead to liberation, while demoniac qualities bind to material existence.

English: The divine qualities lead to liberation, while the demoniac qualities are considered bondage. O son of Pandu, do not grieve, for you are born with divine qualities.

Meaning: Krishna reassures Arjuna that he belongs to the divine path.

Full Explanation: Divine nature uplifts the soul towards freedom and spiritual growth, while demonic nature leads to entanglement. Arjuna is reminded of his noble birth and inner potential.

Prav·πõtti·πÅ cha niv·πõtti·πÅ cha janƒÅ na vidur ƒÅsurƒÅ·∏•,
Na ≈õauca·πÅ nƒÅpi chƒÅchƒÅro na satya·πÅ te·π£u vidyate.

Symbolism: The demoniac lack clarity of action, purity, good conduct, and truth.

English: The demoniac do not know what is to be done or what is not to be done. Neither purity, nor proper conduct, nor truth is found in them.

Meaning: A lack of moral compass defines the demoniac nature.

Full Explanation: Without understanding dharma, demoniac people act impulsively, ignoring cleanliness, discipline, and truth, which are the foundation of righteous living.

Symbolism: Wicked people engage in destructive deeds, bringing harm to the world.
