‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•á‡§§‡•ç ||

Trividham narakasyedam dvƒÅram nƒÅ≈õanam ƒÅtmana·∏•,
KƒÅmah krodhas tathƒÅ lobhas tasmƒÅd etat trayam tyajet.

Symbolism: Desire, anger, and greed are the three gates to self-destruction leading to hell.

English: There are three gates leading to hell‚Äîlust, anger, and greed. Every sane person should abandon these, for they lead to the degradation of the soul.

Meaning: By overcoming desire, anger, and greed, one protects the soul from ruin.

Full Explanation: These three are destructive impulses. The Gita warns that indulging in them leads to downfall, but abandoning them opens the path to peace and liberation.

Daivasura Sampad Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 16.23

‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§É |
‡§® ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç ||

Ya·∏• ≈õƒÅstra-vidhim uts·πõjya vartate kƒÅma-kƒÅrata·∏•,
Na sa siddhim avƒÅpnoti na sukha·πÅ na parƒÅ·πÅ gatim.

Symbolism: Ignoring divine laws and acting out of desire leads to downfall and misery.

English: He who disregards scriptural injunctions and acts according to his desires never attains perfection, happiness, or the supreme goal.

Meaning: Guidance from scriptures is essential; otherwise, desires mislead one to ruin.

Full Explanation: The Gita emphasizes that personal whims, without higher guidance, trap one in ignorance. Only by aligning with dharma can one achieve lasting joy and liberation.

Daivasura Sampad Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 16.24

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•å |
‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø ||

TasmƒÅc chƒÅstra·πÅ pramƒÅ·πáam te kƒÅryƒÅkƒÅrya-vyavasthitau,
J√±ƒÅtvƒÅ ≈õƒÅstra-vidhƒÅnokta·πÅ karma kartum ihƒÅrhasi.

Symbolism: The scriptures are the guiding light to discern right from wrong.

English: Therefore, let the scriptures be your authority in determining what should be done and what should not be done. Knowing what is enjoined in the scriptures, you should act accordingly.

Meaning: Scriptures provide wisdom to differentiate between right and wrong actions.

Full Explanation: This verse concludes the chapter by affirming the authority of dharmic texts. Only by living according to scriptural wisdom can one attain peace, success, and liberation.

Shraddhatraya Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 17.3

‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§ |
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§∏‡§É ||

SattvƒÅnur≈´pƒÅ sarvasya ≈õraddhƒÅ bhavati BhƒÅrata,
≈öraddhƒÅ-mayo ‚Äôya·πÅ puru·π£o yo yacchraddha·∏• sa eva sa·∏•.

Symbolism: A person‚Äôs faith reflects their inner nature; faith shapes destiny.

English: O Bharata, the faith of each is in accordance with their nature. A person is made of faith; whatever one‚Äôs faith is, that indeed they are.

Meaning: Faith is not accidental but arises from one‚Äôs inner disposition.

Explanation: Krishna highlights that faith governs personality and conduct. One becomes what one believes in.

Symbolism: Food, sacrifice, austerity, and charity are all influenced by the three gunas.

English: Even food dear to all is threefold, as are sacrifice, austerity, and charity. Hear the distinctions among them.

Meaning: Everything in life is influenced by sattva, rajas, or tamas.

Explanation: Krishna shows that even daily actions like eating or giving are shaped by the gunas.

Symbolism: Mental discipline, purity of thoughts, and control of self form the highest austerity of the mind.

English: Serenity of mind, gentleness, silence, self-control, and purity of heart‚Äîthese are called austerities of the mind.

Meaning: True mental tapas lies in peace, discipline, and purity of thoughts.

Full Explanation: This shloka explains that the highest mental practice is not outward rituals, but cultivating inner peace, clarity, and noble intentions.

Shraddhatraya Vibhaga Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 17.17

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§®‡§∞‡•à‡§É ‡•§

≈öraddhayƒÅ parayƒÅ tapta·πÅ tapas tat-trividha·πÅ narai·∏•, Aphala-ƒÅkƒÅ·πÖk·π£ibhir yuktai·∏• sƒÅttvika·πÅ paricak·π£ate.

Symbolism: Austerities performed with faith and without expectation of reward are sattvic and pure.

English: The threefold austerity practiced with supreme faith, without desiring reward, is called sattvic.

Meaning: Selfless discipline is the essence of sattva guna.

Full Explanation: When tapas is performed purely out of devotion, without selfish motives, it elevates the soul and brings harmony.

Moksha Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 18.9

‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® |
‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏ ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§É ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§‡§É ||

Symbolism: True renunciation is doing one‚Äôs duty simply because it is right‚Äîfree from attachment and free from craving for results.

English: That work which is performed as one‚Äôs duty, simply because it ought to be done, abandoning attachment and the desire for its fruits‚Äîsuch renunciation is considered sattvic.

Meaning: Do your duty for duty‚Äôs sake, not for reward.

Explanation: Krishna defines the highest kind of renunciation: not running away from action, but letting go of clinginess and result-hunting while acting with clarity and devotion.

Moksha Sannyasa Yoga

Bhagavad Gita 18.11

‡§® ‡§π‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡§æ ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§§‡§É |
‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§´‡§≤‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§∏ ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ||

Na hi dehabh·πõtƒÅ ≈õhakya·πÅ tyaktu·πÅ karmƒÅ·πáy a≈õhe·π£hata·∏•,
Yas tu karma-phala-tyƒÅgƒ´ sa tyƒÅgƒ´ty abhidhƒ´yate.

Symbolism: True renunciation is giving up attachment to the results, not abandoning all actions.

English: It is not possible for an embodied being to renounce all actions completely. But one who gives up attachment to the fruits of actions is truly called a renunciant.

Meaning: Renunciation is about detachment, not inactivity.

Explanation: Krishna clarifies that life demands action, but liberation comes when we let go of attachment to the outcomes.

Symbolism: Every action is driven by five factors ‚Äî the body, the doer, the senses, effort, and divine will.

English: The place of action (body), the doer, the senses, various efforts, and divine providence ‚Äî these are the five causes of all action.

Meaning: No action is solely due to human effort; divine will also plays a role.

Explanation: Recognizing the divine as one factor humbles the ego and prevents pride in our deeds.

Meaning: Divine guidance ensures victory and righteousness.

Explanation: Sanjaya concludes the Gita affirming the eternal triumph of dharma when guided by Krishna‚Äôs wisdom.
